<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Recommended for family with teenagers We stayed at the Argonaut for six nights, family of four with a 14 year old boy and 16 year old girl, in two rooms. We loved the location in a restored brick warehouse directly across the street from the Fisherman's Wharf piers. Great access to historic public transportation - cable car turnaround across the street and the historic street car line a couple of blocks away, which takes you all the way along the Embarcadero and down Market street. Walk to dozens of restaurants and to the Alcatraz and Sausalito Ferries. Friendly staff, helpful concierge. San Francisco National Maritime Park is across the street, and the park visitor center is actually in the hotel building. We walked to Ghirardelli Square, about two blocks away, for nightly chocolate bars (free as you walk in the door) and ice cream sundaes.We stayed in adjacent interior rooms, facing an air shaft rather than the street, which we would recommend both for the price break and because they are a little insulated from hustle and bustle of the tourist district. Nothing is cheap in San Francisco but at $179 per room per night this was only slightly more money than ordinary motels in the area and with a much nicer location and atmosphere. Free high speed internet (wired and wireless) was a big plus with teenagers wanting to stay in touch with home and friends (we brought a laptop). Parking is valet only and pricey, avoid having a car if you can (we needed a car for day trips out of the city).

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great hotel, great location Stayed here from UK for our first holiday away without the kids and were not disapointed! <Author>floridian_kitten
<Content>Impeccable Hospitality! My husband and I had the pleasure of spending the first 3 nights of our recent honeymoon at the Argonaut. We arrived late due to some flight delays, but check-in was efficient and we received everything we had requested at the time of reservation (quiet room away from the elevator, 4th floor, with a view of the bay and Golden Gate Bridge). The bell hop was quick to assist us with our bags and he even brought us a complimentary bottle of wine! The room was very clean, with a large bathroom and very comfortable bed. The window was a little small, which is my only complaint, as the room didn't get much sunlight, and while we had a great view, we had to sit by the window to really take it in. The honor bar was well-stocked and refilled daily. Housekeeping service did a great job keeping our room tidy while we were there. All the hotel staff were very friendly, polite, and made us feel welcome.We ordered room service our first night because we arrived so late and were too tired to venture out for food. Their room service menu after 10pm is quite limited, but the service was prompt and the food was hot and tasty. The hotel's restaurant serves a tasty breakfast, if slightly pricey (even for the area). One morning we were in a hurry, and when we told our server we were running late he rushed our food out and we were done with breakfast in about 15 minutes! We were so impressed with the service there, even moreso than the food (but we do recommend the crab omelette).The location of the hotel is great -- walking distance to Fisherman's Wharf, but far enough away from the main tourist area that it's not so crowded and noisy. The cable cars, Ghirardelli Square, and Buena Vista Cafe are right around the corner. We thoroughly enjoyed our stay there and will definitely return to the Argonaut next time we visit San Francisco.

<Content>Bring your ear plugs! We stayed at the Argonaut hotel for 2 nights and loved every aspect of it apart from the noise level. I need to give credit where it is due. There were shrieks of laughter, loud conversations and we thought at one point of time, cigarette smoke coming from under the adjoining door (it was supposed to be a non-smoking room!). We thought it would end at 10pm but it did not. We alerted the front desk with our concerns but it did not work. I called again just before 11pm when it became aparent that we would not be able to sleep and requested a room change. The front desk was very courteous and kindly gave us a quieter room but at that time, the damage had been done. My wife and I found it difficult to fall asleep after that. So our 2nd night was pretty much ruined.We informed the front desk again in the morning of our dissatisfaction that we were made to suffer when it was neightbours who were being inconsiderate. The response we got from the front desk was sorry...it is an old hotel. Hardly satisfactory at all. I would have loved to address this to the manager but our shuttle arrived at that time.So, it is a game of Russian roulette I think. If you are lucky, you would get considerate neighbors who would keep the noise down. Otherwise, bring a pair of ear plugs.But the location of the hotel was unbeatable.

Being at the Aquatic Park end of Fisherman's Wharf, it is removed from the hustle  bustle of the kitsch. Being a re-habbed historical property and the location of the visitor's center for the San Francisco Maritime National Historic Park, it's the perfect place to begin one's exploration of the entire Fisherman's Wharf/Golden Gate area. Ghirardelli Square is immediately past the Cable Car turnaround.The Cable Cars have a line ending just beyond the hotel, and the historic streetcars are available just two blocks east. Getting around town is very easy from this hotel. In fact, our entire visit used public transportation: BART from the airport to downtown, and a streetcar along the Embarcadero to the hotel; then reversing for departure.We found excellent restaurants in the area immediately around the hotel.During your time in the lobby..., ponder the operation of the timepiece above the fireplace. We could not have been more pleased. The concierge was helpful and the wine reception every evening is a nice touch. We never had any trouble with the valet service, the wait for our car each time was not excessive. The parking fee each night was $36 and there is no other option, but, keep in mind this is San Francisco and there is no free or budget parking. I'm sure if you check with other properties in the area this is a competitive rate. Also, I didn't see any other fisherman's wharf hotels that seemed as nice as the Argonaut. The location is great-within walking distance to all of the Fisherman's Wharf attractions, Ghiradelli Square is right around the corner, Lombard Street is four or five block up the hill and don't miss The Buena Vista around the corner for an Irish coffee!I would definately stay again at this property and will recommend it to all my friends.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Don't Believe the Negative Reviews My wife  I spent a week here, on the 4th floor with a view of the bay  Ghirardelli Square. First - the staff was great. Everyone was extremely friendly and very helpful. I understand that a guest may encounter an employee on a bad day, but don't let that color your opinion of the staff overall.Second - The room was great. I suggest the 4th floor, as there is no one walking above you. Also, I suggest paying the extra for the view rooms, even if you don't plan to spend too much time in the room (otherwise you get a view of a tiny concrete courtyard, not too great). While other reviews mentioned noise outside, my wife  I didn't notice anything more than the occasional cable car bell. Yes, the room is somewhat small - but folks, this is a hotel. If I want bigger rooms, I'll stay home. How much space do you need to sleep and brush your teeth (and maybe shower once in a while)? The only issue I had, and this is minor, was the somewhat thin walls between rooms and the hallway. Some noise can be heard from adjacent rooms and the hall outside the door. But this was in no way a deal-breaker.Third - Great location. I don't like the idea of being stuck in the middle of all the buildings downtown or in other more congested areas of the city. This hotel's spot on Fisherman's Wharf was perfect for me, as I prefer being close to the water. If we wanted to go into town, we either drove or took the trolley. There are plenty of excellent restaurants within walking distance of this hotel; likewise Pier 39  Ghirardelli Square are nearby.Absolutely do not hesitate to book a room at the Argonaut, as long as you're looking to stay in the Fisherman's Wharf area. If you drive to San Francisco, be ready for the $36 per night parking fee. They will bring your car to the front door whenever you request however. And you will find similar costs at other hotels. Otherwise, this hotel should be on your very short list of places to stay in San Francisco. You will not be disappointed.By the way - I rarely, if ever, review places/things/experiences I've encountered. But the great experience my wife  I had on our vacation compelled me to do so in this case.

<Author>Olliebuba
<Content>Nice Hotel, Great Location Great location close and/or easily accessible to fun activities in San Franciso. Directly across the street from the cable cars with easy access to downtown and Chinatown. Within walking distance to Ghiradelli Square, Fisherman's Wharf and Pier 39. Much safer than hotels located in Union Square area. Hotel decor was beautiful, similar to being on a cruise ship, with great wine gathering each evening at 5 p.m. Rooms were small and narrow. Rooms on the interior face other rooms, with no view. Rooms on the exterior face bay, cannery or park. Cannery side is noisy during the day and evening, even on the higher levels. Fourth floor rooms do not have old wood decor like other levels. Most of the staff is very friendly, however, some have an attitude that borders on arrogance. Overall a nice hotel, but I would hesitate to pay the higher price for the Cannery or Park View rooms versus the interior rooms.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>We loved every minute of our stay! I was in San Francisco for a conference  my daughter flew out to meet me on the last day. There are so many hotels to choose from in the bay area, it was overwelming. A family friend who lives in Oakland recommended the Argonaut, as her company put her up there when she moved to CA. We could not have picked a more wonderful hotel!! The staff is terrific, not at all snobby like you find in so many big cities. We used the concierge services every morning to help plan our day  directions for getting around. Our room was always very clean  up-to-date with amenities. The Blue Mermaid restaurant adjacent to the hotel is marvelous. We could jump on the cable car across the way for quick access to the city. If you stay at the other hotels I saw located at Fisherman's Wharf, you have to deal have all the tourist traffic  confusion (we were there over an extended weekend) but the Argonaut is at the end of the wharf where you don't get all the noise  street people, yet it's within easy walking distance. We even made it to one of the 5-6 p.m. wine receptions they offer daily in the lobby (Australian wines were being served that evening) - cool idea, very relaxing,  you will meet other guests from all over the country. I spend fifteen years in the hotel business in the 80's  90's  all I can say is: great choice, you won't regret it!

<Author>Radu Toma
<Content>Good hotel, but overrated and overpriced Stayed here for 2 nights for our anniversary in february. Location wise, it does not get any better if you want to stay in Fisherman's Wharf. Price, at $145/ night (on special on hotels.(-)) is just about right. At $220-$800, as advertised on the hotel's site and all other sites we found rooms on (Expedia, Orbitz, etc) it is way overpriced! Everything works in the room and is good quality, from the king size mattress to the Sony TV, the Starbucks coffee in the room, 3 different papers in the morning and complementary bottle of wine (was it for our anniversary, that I told them about??). However, while the rooms have character, they are much smaller than they seem in pictures, the bathroom is no better than in a 2-3 star hotel and most of the the windows (who don't open) face other windows! Lobby and hallways are not more impressive either, and front desk staff, while polite, seemed somewhat inexperienced. If you can get it below $150, it's definitely worth it. If not, go for another area, like Nob Hill, or Union Square, where you get more for the money.

<Author>MGMarch
<Content>Great value in San Francisco We spent three nights (Fri-Sun) at the Argonaut in mid-January as part of a SF to LA vacation. We were extremely pleased with the experience, especially the friendliness of the staff. For $199/night booked through the Kimpton web site, we found the Argonaut to be a great value in an expensive city.Having lived in San Francisco years ago, I was hesitant to choose a place near Fisherman's Wharf. We were travelling with two teenagers who I figured would enjoy the wharf for an hour or two before getting totally bored. Did I really want to be stuck down at the Wharf? In a word, yes. Because we weren't stuck. San Francisco is one of the easiest big cities to get around (though it isn't cheap).On Friday, we walked to Ghiradelli Square for lunch and a great bay view. Then we took the obligatory cable car ride -- starting literally steps from the hotel's front door -- to Union Square for shopping and sight-seeing. On Saturday, we picked up a rental car (to use on the drive to LA). While I was concerned about the cost of parking, I was more concerned about the exhorbitant cab fares in San Francisco. One round-trip cab fare would equal the $36/night parking fee. My concern about parking was alleviated the first day when one of the several helpful doormen tipped me off that there was plenty of on-street parking nearby and that you could leave your car there until 10 a.m. I was able to find a spot right next to the hotel on Hyde Street both nights we had the car.With the parking issue dealt with, we used the car to drive all around the area -- from Telegraph Hill to Twin Peaks to Berkeley to Fort Point to the beaches to Haight Ashbury to Muir Woods. And getting back to the Argonaut was always easy. And you can't beat the location for cruising the Wharf from Pier 39 all the way to Ghiradelli, tacky gift shops and all.As you can tell, we were not in the hotel too much, but when we were the experience was excellent. We checked in early (about noon) and were given a room way in the back of the hotel which was too far for my wife to walk to the elevator. We requested another room but none was available at the time, so we checked our bags and went off to Union Square. When we got back around 6 p.m., we were given a near replica of the room we were offered before but much nearer the elevator. The room was extremely spacious, clean and well appointed with a high ceiling and complimentary Internet access. It overlooked a patio area in the Cannery, which we viewed with a little trepidation. But aside from an odd bit of loud music one morning from one of the bar/cafes, it wasn't a problem. The fact is, they pretty much roll up the sidewalks on this area of the wharf at 10 p.m. in the winter months.One big concern I had from posts on TripAdvisor was the thin walls. While we did not encounter any big issues with this, I can see how a noisy neighbor could pose a problem. One night our neighbor had a pretty rough cough, which was easily audible, but fortunately not so disruptive as to prevent us from sleeping.I am not big at staying at the same hotel time and again, but I would be hard pressed not to return to the Argonaut. The location is perfect and the staff is outstanding.

<Author>starbuck212
<Content>Unique, Fun, and Quality I recently stayed at The Argonaut Hotel in Fisherman's Warf area of San Francisco for 3 nights in Jan. I was very pleasantly surprised with the uniqueness and quality of the hotel. Let me start off by saying that I consider myself to be a hotel snob. I travel a lot for work so I'm used to staying in nicer places. Marriott/ Hyatt are usually standards for me. So I was nervous when I decided to veer off the Hyatt/ Marriott hotel path and try something new. I found out about The Argonaut hotel when I did a random search on the internet for Fisherman's Warf hotels. The description said it was one of the newer hotels in Fisherman's Warf and it seemed more unique than a Marriott or other standard hotel. So we gave it a try. The decor of the hotel is so much fun! I was afraid that it would be to kiddy, but instead I thought that the lobby was very tastefully decorated all in a nautical theme. We arrived at 5:30 and were able to participate in the nightly wine hour. The lobby gets packed from 5-6!The hotel hallways and rooms were very cute and vibrant, still with the nautical theme. I loved the decor and the extra touches in the room -- loved the Aveda products in the bathroom, thought the leapord print robes were fun, loved the Sony cd alarmclock, loved the funky lamps, loved the huge power outlet thing on the desk that could hold like six different plugs, loved the huge nautical mirror, loved the shutters, loved the brick wall. Also loved the bedding. Very high quality, very comfortable. We had a room that over looked Hyde street and could see the Golden Gate bridge. I thought it was worth the few extra bucks / night to have a bay view (even though it was more of a street view than a bay view), bc the interior rooms just looked out onto a square in the middle of the hotel where you could see everyone elses interior rooms. This hotel's location is PRIME!!! It is ON the main drag in Fisherman's Warf, not a block or two away like all the other hotels in that area. It is also the closest hotel to Ghiardelli Square (walking distance) and the closest hotel to the Hyde  Powell Trolley line (stone throw away). I would definitely stay there again and would also stay at any other Kimpton Hotel after having enjoyed this visit so much.

<Author>SactoSteph
<Content>Great Location..Updated  My family stayed at this property Dec 9-11th,2005 with intentions of enjoying holiday festivities in SFO. We paid $134/nt through ----, thanks to TripAdvisor!The exterior photos of this property make it look dated.. walking inside, it's immediately apparent EVERYTHING is new and modern. Entirely nautically themed..from sailboats in the lobby, portholes in the elevator lobby, to the nautical museum next door..the property has flair. Original exterior brick and large structural wood beams are all that remain of the original cannery structure that now houses the hotel. They add some great character.Our room (#220) was long and relatively narrow. Uniquely, our door opened out into the hallway. We didn't get a bathtub, and had an exterior-facing room whose one large window was at shin-level of passing pedestrians. Because it's new, everything works great -- great phones, nice Sony swiveling TVs, an honor bar, great shower pressure and efficient temperature controls. (One note, don't keep the fan on ON - our daughter switched it and we were dried out after a night of constant air blowing..)The room has SUPER comfortable beds, pillows and great linens. I was impressed. The only interactions we had were with the valets. We found them friendly on the way in; surly on the way out. The location is terrific. We walked one block up the hill (past our room) and took the cable car to Union Square for breakfast at the Chancellor Hotel (YUM!). The park next to the property (where the cable cars turn around) affords terrific views of Alcatraz and the GG Bridge. Immediately next to the property is their restaurant The Blue Mermaid. We tried their NE Clam Chowder and the Sausage one..finding both to be disappointments. We did not try the room service or other meals there as there's a ton of restaurants around the hotel.Next to the Blue Mermaid, The Cannery shopping area courtyard is pretty neat. We heard some great live music and enjoyed some homemade ice cream within. We walked along Embarcadero and viewed lots of unpleasant tourist trappings..lots of restaurants and enjoyed the bread baking factory of Bourdin. It's a can't miss seeing the sunset beyind Alcatraz!

<Author>L8H
<Content>This hotel has character and the wow factor! Myself and my wife have just returned from a 5 day break in San Francisco and stayed at the Argonaut Hotel. We picked the hotel based on it's top 10 status on Trip Advisor. We were not disappointed, this hotel has loads of character and is one of the best US hotels we have stayed in.The location is surperb which all the previous reviews confirm. It is just around the corner to the Hyde/Powell cable car turnaround point and only a short walk from the Hyde/Market cable car and also the streetcar service which goes right away to Castro. The ferry piers are also within easy reach. There is an abundance of restaurants/cafes/shops etc. Definately try the fresh crab from anywhere on Fishermans Grotto and the fresh clam chowder in a bread bowl from the boudin bakery.The check in was quick, painless and pleasant experience. The hotel decor was nautical, modern, cosy and very well kept. The room was like it hadnt been slept in before and was spotlessly clean. We had an inside room with a view of an inner square. The room was longer than wide but plenty of room for two with a lovely nautical theme and exposed beams left behind by its previous use as the Del Monte warehouse. The room had a Sony Vega TV and DVD player, radio alarm clock and Aveda products in the bathrooms, umbrella in the wardrobe/closet (which we needed one day) and dont forget the quirky leopard print bathrobes.Every night at 17:00 there is free wine provided of the monthly featured vineyard by the hotel manager and staff. It can get a bit busy in the lobby and fire area during these times but it is good to mingle with fellow guest and staff to swap stories and tips.All staff we came in contact with were friendly, helpful and always had something nice to say such as welcome back, Hope you had a nice day or Have a great day. There was an asian girl who worked on the concierge desk who wasnt rude or unhelpful but not has friendly looking as the others.All in all this hotel is clean, efficient, quirky, cosy and has bags of character. we will definately return to SF and when we do there is no doubt that we will stay at The Argonaught.Some tips which you may find useful. Buy the Muni pass for transport on the Cable cars, streetcars and buses, it will save you a fortune. We paid $24 for 7 days and had our monies worth and more despite not using 2 days of the pass. Go to Mamas on Washington Square for breakfast, you have to queue for 15-20mins but it is worth it. More locally is the Hollywood Cafe run by a chinese husband and wife due. Great american breakfast great service and you get to leave a message on a napkin for the wall. Do a wine country tour it is good to get out of SF and have a few! sips of wine. If you go to Alcatraz have the audio tour included its worth it and very interesting. Take a door to door shuttle to and from airport costs around $10-$13 each, buts it worth it. We tried to do public transport, we caught BART from airport costing $5 each plus a cable car to the hotel at $5 each. It took over an hour and was a bit of hastle with the cases, for another $10 we had a shuttle back, which was quicker and easier.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice Place, Excellent Location, a few rough edges My wife and I stayed at the Argonaut for a week.You can't beat the location for a sight-seeing vacation. The hotel is located at the western edge of the Fisherman's Wharf area - out of the middle of the hubbub but close enough to walk to everything along the waterfront. The farthest waterfront destination that we visited was the Ferry building, and that's just a short trip on the F-line streetcars. The Powell-Hyde cable car turnaround is across the street and Ghirardelli Square is just a block farther. LOTS of restaurants within a 5-10 minute walk. Everything else is just a walk, cable car or streetcar ride away.The rooms are in excellent condition and well cared for. We stayed in a double Queen with bay view - and there was a lot more room between the furniture and walls than most hotels. Housekeeping does a good job on each room daily. The WEGA TVs and DVD players make for nearly infinite viewing choices (a WB station on the list would be a good addition).There are still a few quirks that the hotel needs to work out:1. The walls ARE a bit thin - if you have a loud neighbor you will know it. They could have knocked a few square feet off the room to make the walls thicker.2. The check-in area gets crowded in the evenings, and the folks behind the desk are a bit snooty. (The rest of the staff is fine)3. The business center PC/Printer combinations are expensive ($24/hour) and not well maintained. They should provide a printer-only solution with a USB connection and WiFi or Ethernet network connection so that we can use OUR laptops. It galls one to have to pay $6 just to print a boarding pass and have to fix the printer to boot. The free Ethernet internet connection in the rooms worked very well.One cautionary note - the room safes are easy to use and will probably hold a standard size laptop but modern wide-screen laptops don't fit. Buy a laptop cable lock and put it on the shelf locked around the hangar bar.

<Author>DCFrequentFlier
<Content>Loved this hotel The Argonaut is located in Fisherman's Wharf by the water. It is charming with a cool nautical theme and a great staff. The hotel is very accommodating. We booked rooms for a short two night stay but then decided to spend our second night in Napa. The hotel desk staff graciously canceled our second night without penalty. We reserved two rooms, an interior queen and a deluxe room. The queen, as expected, was very small although the decor made up for the size. The deluxe room had a 'view' but unfortunately our window looked into the scaffolding of the building across the street. When you stay there, request a higher floor (3rd or higher) facing the water. Also, the Argonaut offers a lot of 'package' deals. If you are driving a car, check out the deals that come with parking. The hotel charges $36 a night for parking (I parked on the street to save the charge and the bellman still walked over to my car and helped me with my bags. Gotta love this hotel). A rate that includes parking is often a better option than a regular room rate (the packages also include breakfast etc). Fisherman's Wharf is one big tourist trap so the area is deserted at night.. but you can get to other neighborhoods quickly. Avoid eating in the area.. food is not great and charges are high. Snag a cab or the cable car to another neighborhood and get a great meal for a lot less. During the day, its an interesting area to walk around.. and again, you can grab a cable car and visit other neighborhoods. I am a big fan of the Kimpton hotels and this ia a great one. The decor makes it a lot of fun. I'd recommend it and I'll plan to stay there again in the future.

<Author>lass=
<Content>Best Hotel (by far) in Fisherman's Wharf My teenage daughter and I stayed in the Argonaut Hotel for two nights. I chose the Fisherman's Wharf area because of all of the things to do, especially the Alcatraz tour. The Argonaut is a historical hotel that was originally the Del Monte warehouse in the early 1900's. It is directly across the historical Del Monte Cannery. They did a very good job of keeping the historical integrity of the hotel intact. The original beams and brick walls are exposed in the rooms. The service was excellent! EVERYONE was friendly- what a nice surprise. I guess I am just used to the east-coast grumpiness. The doormen(plural) would open the door almost every time, and say, Hi, how are you doing today? The beds were ultra-comfy. The bathrooms were very nice and offered Aveda bath ammenities(the counter-tops were big enough, and don't know what the earlier reviewer had brought with them that didn't fit!)There was also Starbuck's coffee for the coffee maker (bring your own creamers though as they offered only 2 small packets of a generic powdered creamer.) The Argonaut had a nice ,uncrowded,work-out room which came in handy after eating the Ghiardelli chocolate earlier that day. The Powell-Hyde cable car turntable was right around the corner- pricey but worth it if you actually used it as a means of transportation. Costs $5 one-way, $10 round-trip and $11 for a day pass. The Alcatraz night-tour was great. Was a cold and rainy night but added to the dreary history of Alcatraz. We didn't use the audio tour, and chose to venture around the building by ourselves and away from all the people taking the tour. Be prepared to be trapped on the island for 3 hours though. One last thing that I recommend doing while in the San Francisco area and if you have a car- go to the Winchester Mystery House in San Jose- it is worth the trip. Again, the Argonaut was the BEST hotel in Fisherman's Wharf. It is a Kimpton Hotel and I would definitely stay there again and be more likely to stay in a Kimpton Hotel after our stay. If you are a AAA member, you will be pleasantly surprised with the rates offered.

<Author>oxfordshireboy
<Content>Interesting, distinctive and high-quality hotel Contrary to the review below which described it as an ordinary hotel which only has nice location - I couldn't disagree more. I am used to staying in Hiltons, Sheratons, Marriotts on business - they have a high level of service but are almost always completely ubiquitous and utterly dull. By contrast, the Argonaut is a breath of fresh air - it is a really pleasant, attractive and stimulating place to stay, the kind of place I choose to stay for leisure rather than work. Staff are friendly and interesting whilst delivering the high-quality service one expects at this price - none of the obsequious-yet-disinterested vibe found at many other chain hotels. All the basics are as one would expect, and the big Sony TV and DVD in the room is a nice touch. Food is excellent, and the courtyard tables with the buskers outside is a very nice place to unwind. Only minor downside is the location - Fisherman's Wharf is a dire neon-and-plastic tourist trap, with only pretty views of the Bay and fresh fish stalls to redeem it. A tasteful and refined hotel seems quite out-of-place here! But the Argonaut is exactly that.

<Author>lightbulb03
<Content>Awesome Place to stay waterfront at the wharf This hotel was quite a find. Our objective was to stay as close to the waterfront as we could and we sure picked the perfect place. This hotel is a converted warehouse as part of the Cannery next door. It is located on the corner of Hyde and Jefferson directly across from the Hyde Street Pier and across the street from the Hyde/Powell Cable Car terminal/turn-around. This is all part of the maritime park and museum directly across from Ghirardelli Square and within easy walking from the hotel. What a beautiful area. We had easy access to the wharf, cannery mall, ghirardelli square, walking paths, views of Golden Gate and Alcatraz. The hotel staff treated us very warmly and always said hello. The room was large and the view was a deluxe view of Alcatraz and Hyde Street Pier. The street below was always busy but since there weren't large buildings across the street we didn't mind because of the great views. The hotel has a restaurant (the blue mermaid) which was ok. We ate outside one night and they provided tall propane heaters to ward off the chill of the evening breeze. The service was a little slow and forgetful and there was a language barrier at breakfast. Toast came instead of french toast.All in all a wonderful experience. The staff bent over backwards to make us feel at home. I'd stay here again definitely.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A Pleasure! Just returned with my family after 3 nights at the Argonaut. It's in the heart of Fisherman's Wharf - very convenient. The hotel is a very unique experience: funky decor, very friendly staff. Some of the rooms have 2 queen beds which makes travelling with families easier. The rooms are BIG! VERY comfortable beds! Great TV and DVD player for the kids. The bellman really went out of his way to help us get out of town on the day of a major bike race when the streets around the hotel were blocked. The only bad thing is the location: Fisherman's Wharf is a seedy place filled with homeless beggars and endless stores hawking cheap t-shirts and sunglasses. This area is definitely a tourist trap but may be worth a few days stay to look around. The only good things are the local museums and piers dealing with naval history - they're great. The Argonaut is a jewel of a hotel and was a pleasure to return to at the end of the day.

<Author>krohrig
<Content>Fantastic Hotel! My sister and I just got back from staying at the Argonaut 09/3 - 09/05. This hotel is right in Fisherman's Wharf. Perfectly located. We've always wanted to stay there but knew the hotel rate was a little high. I got this fantastic deal from Travelocity where if I book my hotel and airfare together they would take off $75.00. It was a steal! We arrived at the hotel about 9:00 AM Saturday morning. They checked us right in. I thought we would have to wait. Our room was hugh. The decor was a nautical theme. Very nicely done. The room's necessities were ironing board, hair dryer, two bathrobes, there were bathing products by Aveda, The shampoo was rosemary mint. Very delightful. There were plenty of towels. The room had two queen size beds that were so comfortable I don't think I moved the whole night. The pillows were very soft. Our room overlooked the courtyard where there were restaurants. It was never loud at night. We both slept very comfortably. There is a wine reception at 5:00 PM... get there a little earlier to get a seat. We arrived at SFO. We took the bart to the embarcadero and then hopped on the F Line bus that dropped us off about 3 blocks from our hotel. Total cost per person was $6.50. We got to the hotel very quickly. There is internet hookups in the room. There is a cable car turnaround about one block away. We recommend having Irish coffee at the Buena Vista which is one block away. Right across the street from the cable car turnaround. We had breakfast at Joannies which is through the courtyard and across the street for breakfast. Since our flight was so early Monday morning we took a shuttle which only cost us $13.00 each. I will definitely look for specials to this hotel again! Very satisfied.

<Author>Mr.Mom
<Content>Arrived, hating it! Left, loving it! I did not want to stay at this hotel in this part of San Francisco. I'm a Four Seasons kind of guy where I know it is going to be safe, clean and kid friendly. Although not much character you usually know what you are getting with a Four Seasons or other upscale chain. My wife is the total opposite. She prefers character over luxury. So, I reluctantly agreed to stay at the Argonaut. The hotel is on a very touristy, crowded street. Quiet, it is not. The location if fine for everything around the wharf and even Lombard street is pretty close, but that's all. All other attractions are a bus, cable car, or taxi ride, away. The cable car station is accross the street from the hotel but get there early to avoid a long (1-2 hour) line. Just outside the hotel is the Cannery where outside every evening they have live music until 10PM. It was very loud in our room but not as loud as movie night on Sundays. They have an outdoor screening of a movie every Sunday and it is louder than the live music and it went on until 10:40pm. I thought the hotel was not kid friendly at all. No activities, pool, game room, gift shop or anything. Just a treasure chest filled with cheap little toys by the front desk. But so much for my opinion because our kids loved the hotel. The staff were very, very friendly and helpful. The concierge was Fantastic. The rooms are noisy from outside noise and adjacent rooms but its all part of the character. The rooms were not so small. They were very comfortable for a family of 4. It is a four star hotel and it truly felt like it was. I highly recommend this hotel. The next time we go to San Francisco we will not stay here only because I would like to try a different part of town. But for 1st timers this is a great place and we will stay here again. Some day. PS: ask about The Big Red Shiny Mack Fire Engine.

<Author>Puppysmoocher
<Content>A Wonderfully Unique Hotel Stay My husband and I traveled to the Argonaut Hotel with my parents, my husband's mother, sister, niece, brother and sister-in-law - plus our German Shepherd, Cleo, who is a service animal. We had three rooms, including a Bayview Suite, which comfortably slept 4 adults and one child (King-size bed in bedroom with rollaway and pullout sofa in the living room with a door separating the two spaces). This suite had a view of Alcatraz, the Golden Gate Bridge and Ghirardelli Square (Room #345). It also had a dining room table that easily sat 6 people and a refrigerator with enough room to add our treasures' that we brought back from our outings (chocolates, wines  doggy bags from various restaurants). The Jacuzzi tub in the suite's bathroom overlooked the bay with a separate shower area. At $770 a night, it would be a reasonable alternative for two couples interested in having more room to move about as well as the best view in the hotel. The King Bay-view room that my husband and I upgraded to, also had a view of the Golden Gate Bridge and Ghirardelli Square. The Cable Car turn-around was right outside our window in the park across the street (Room #322). Upon check-in I was told that this room was slightly larger than most and judging by the pictures I鈥檝e seen on this site, I think it's true. My parent's room with two full beds was a bit smaller but still had the same view as our room.Everyone from the bellmen to the front desk to the restaurant staff at the Blue Mermaid was exceptionally friendly as well as professional. With two older ladies in wheelchairs, a service dog, three rooms and two cars that needed to be valeted, we had quite a group! The Argonaut staff handled all of us with aplomb and ease. Our cars were always waiting at the curb together. The bellmen assisted both moms in and out of the cars and helped get the wheelchairs in and out of the trunks of the cars. Everyone enjoyed the wine reception in the lobby of the hotel each evening and the staff at the Blue Mermaid would happily pack up meals for some of our guests that didn't make it down to the restaurant for a meal (and deliver it to the room, if we asked). My favorite was the intimate little beer garden at the Blue Mermaid where they fired up their portable heaters when it got a bit chilly outside. On our last evening there, they were showing an old Hollywood movie outside while serving food and drinks. We mentioned how clever we thought it was and the manager told us they had just started doing that every Sunday night. A very nice touch!Check in and check out was a breeze. The rooms were spotless. The beds were extremely comfortable. Everyone that worked at the Argonaut seemed genuinely happy to be there and that was reflected in their smiles and willingness to help in any way they could.A+++, Argonaut!On a side note: the Argonaut Hotel allows pets, not just service animals. There is a great little park right across the street from the hotel where I walked Cleo each morning. There is also a little beach and a pier that was just perfect for an early morning stroll/jog. Pier 39 is only 6 blocks away - an easy stroll past shops and food and fun!

<Author>Traveler111Stamford
<Content>Great Place and Worth the money My wife, teenage daughter and I stayed here at the end of July 2005. Overall, this is a great place with great location, beautiful decor, outstanding service and unique, spacious rooms (ours also had a direct view of Alcatraz and a glimpse of the Golden Gate Bridge).Employees are friendly and greet you when entering the hotel. Kevin, one of the bellmen, was probably the best service provider we have ever experienced. He was very funny, answered our questions and offered honest advice of places to see. We ate at the hotel restaurant, The Blue Mermaid, and found it to a charming room, with great service but with very average food. The major weak spot at the hotel was the concierge staff. They lacked basic knowledge of the area and seemed indifferent about helping us. As a result, we avoided them after interacting with 2 different members of the concierge staff on 2 different days. I found out later that the concierge group is outsourced to a private firm so the concierge employees are not actually employees of the Argonaut Hotel--it's too bad since they are well below the high service quality found elsewhere at the hotel.I wrote my comments on their feedback form and received a personal note a few days later thanking me for my comments--they clearly get the service concept.We would definitely return here-- it was worth paying more to stay here given the experience.

Just go across the street to purchase day or multi-day passes. The hotel was adorable - my kids particularly loved the cheetah bathrobes and the room was a good size, comfy beds and fine amenities. We ate breakfast in the adjoining resturaunt and the food was very good.Our room adjoined another room. The people in the other room were very very loud and obnoxious very early in the morning. We called the front desk, who said they'd call the neighbors, but they never did and the people never stopped the racket. I was not satisfied with the front desk response when I explained this to them upon checkout - however, after sending an email to the hotel, they made every effort to rectify the situation and make sure I was a satisifed customer in the end. They wound up giving me a $100 refund back on my credit card with a follow up note from the manager. This shows goodwill from the management team and shows that customer satisfaction is definitely very important to them..Word of note - the cable car end of line is right across the stree. The lines can take a VERY long time, so if you want to ride the cable car, walk up a few blocks and wait for the cable car. You can usually squeeze on then.We would definitely stay at the Argonaut again!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Wonderful time My family and I spent June 25 through 27 at the Argonaut and loved it. We were steered here by the reviews on Trip Advisor and we knew we made the right choice. First of all is the location... right on Fisherman's Wharf and one block from the Powell and Hyde cable car stop. It is located towards the Golden Gate side of the wharf, near its end and away from the wharf bustle, but certainly close enough to enjoy everything. The hotel was spotless and the staff very attentive and personable. The only minor glitch was a slight delay in having our bags arrive to our room, but this was very minor. The hotel has a very nautical theme to it which we found charming. If a theme hotel is not your bag, then reconsider the choice, but reconsider with much hesitation. A recent review criticized how tacky the theme was. Well, considering that every site that lists the hotel (including its own web site) mentions the heavy nautical theme, the reviewer should have realized this before booking. You get alot for the price of the room and considering how expensive SF is, there is alot to be said for that. Although there is no pool or other significant child oriented stuff, my 11 and 8 year olds loved the hotel, especially for its nautical orientation. Kids are certainly not out of place in this boutique-style hotel. There is a restaurant on site which serves breakfast, lunch, and dinner. The food was fine, but a tad pricey.You definitely need to explore more of the wharf and the city to get better food. Parking is also expensive - forty bucks a day including tax, but parking is a premium in SF. Would definitely stay here again.

<Author>MrAbruzzo
<Content>A Wonderful Stay Stayed here 5 nights and had a wonderful time. The hotel is located near Pier 47, which is actually quite good because while you are within walking distance of Fisherman's Wharf and Pier 39 with all of its shops and restaurants, you are far enough away from the hustle and bustle to enjoy a little serenity. The best part about this hotel is its staff. They are friendly, courteous and willing to help. They always have a smile and hello for you. The rooms are well apportioned and very clean. You have a decent sized bathroom and all the necessary amenities. Try not to get a room with an interior view. You are basically looking at empty space. It's pretty awful. We had a room with an exterior view overlooking the Cannery with both the TransAmerica Tower and Coit Hill in the background. For breakfast, I would recommend either Lori's Diner in Ghiradelli Square or Joanie's around the corner, both are within a five minute walk. There is a restaurant attached to the hotel, the Blue Mermaid. We had breakfast there the first morning. It was okay at best. The Powell-Hyde cable car turnaround is right next to the hotel. This will lead all the way down to Union Square. Mornings and early afternoon are the best time to catch a cable car from this location as the wait can reach excess of an hour later in the day and early evening. You might actually be better off walking down a stop or two and hopping on a car there then waiting in line. The cars tend not to leave fully packed. There are numerous restaurants in the area. I would recommend walking down Columbus Avenue toward Little Italy, there many restaurants and cafes well worth your time. San Francisco is a great city to visit and the Argonaut is an excellent place to stay.

<Author>LAWheels
<Content>An Enjoyable Stay at the Argonaut My wife and I, along with her parents, stayed at the Argonaut for 4 nights in March of this year. I was traveling on business while the rest of the folks were playing tourist. The staff of the hotel was helpful and friendly during our stay. Despite our late check in (11 p.m.), everything went well with the bellman, valet parking ($36 per night, not including tax) and the front desk staff. Also, they gave us a late check out at 1:30 p.m. without a hassle.The rooms featured a nautical theme, which was somewhat SpongeBob Squarepants in appearance but it's all new so it was fine. The rooms aren't wide at about 10' across but they are deep. Our rooms looked out over the Cannery, which was okay. Interior rooms, however, would have a view of a wall with windows in it about 20' away. We'd recommend that you get an outer room, if possible.The hotel was quiet at night, which was a surprise given the number of kids and families that were there and the outdoor activity at the Cannery (restaurants and shops). The bed was quite comfortable and ranked right up there as one of the most comfortable hotel beds that I've slept on. The hotel offered high-speed internet access as well as a fairly comfortable chair and desk set up. The family tried the hotel restaurant for breakfast but it turned out to be a disappointment. We'd recommend that you eat out while there. The surrounding area has a bunch of restaurants of varying quality (Starbucks is nearby, too). For dinner, Scoma's is a good, but pricey, alternative.The first morning there, I exited the hotel and looked for a cab but there were none in sight. The doorman then informed me that a complimentary shuttle was available for trips downtown from 7 a.m. to 9 a.m. The shuttle turned out to be a chauffered Lincoln town car that was available on a first-come, first-serve basis. This came at a complete surprise to me. I used this service two of the three mornings that I was there and it was great. From a wheelchair-accessibility standpoint (my wife is in a wheelchair full-time), the hotel is quite accessible. The front entrance is flat as is access to the front desk and the room itself. The hotel has two large elevators. The room was accessible as well. The bathroom was large and featured a roll-in shower that was as good as you'd find anywhere. It had grab bars and a fold down seat. The hotel also offered (on request) a small, portable shower chair, which turned out to be more stable than the one that we brought with us. The toilet was raised, per ADA standards, and there were grab bars around it. The sink was wall-hung so the wheelchair was able to scoot under it with no problem. On the downside, the carpet in the room (and in the hallways) has a thick pad underneath so my wife had difficulty in moving around the room under her own power. In addition, the bed was too high so transfers were a little dicey. As for the surrounding area, Fisherman's Wharf and Pier 39 are wheelchair accessible but, once you head inland, it's all uphill (it's SF). We were able to make it uphill for one block but did not try to make it up the next steep hill to Ghiradelli Square. There was a lift in a garage that, supposedly, was able to get you up to the garage elevator (which would then take you up to the Square) but there was no call button nor was it manned by anyone. If you want to tour additional areas of SF by wheelchair, a car rental or accessible taxi would be the way to go from this hotel.All in all, we found the Argonaut to be an excellent choice for both business and pleasure and would recommend it for visitors to SF. The price of our rooms was cheaper than what you'd find in most other quality hotels in the city so it was a good value. Just remember that it is in the most touristy area of SF so you get both the benefits and the negatives of that activity.My apologies for the long-winded review but I thought I'd get as much info as I could out for fellow travelers.  
<Date>Apr 18, 2005
<Rating>4	5	4	-1	5	-1	4	-1	

<Author>SuzInAZ1950
<Content>Pretty Great Room We just returned from our stay at the Argonaut over the weekend (4/15-17), and must say, we will return again next year. We chose the Argonaut this time because of its location at the Wharf - most everything we do is in this area, and we didn't want to waste time and money traveling from a hotel outside the area. Unlike the other viewer, one of the reasons I chose the hotel was because of the nautical theme - something definitely out of the ordinary. As far as Disney looking, I've stayed in Disney hotels and they are cramped and ridiculously priced, and not half as cute. We didn't have sticker shock over the price of the room, I guess because we live in Phoenix where rooms in season are well over $500. We got a king bay view room, and were also placed in the wrong room when we checked in (we checked in with Vaughn), but as soon as we called the front desk, they were extremely courteous about putting us in the correct room. The view wasn't all that great, looking out on a construction site which was definitely not the Argonaut's fault. On the other hand to have A GREAT VIEW, we could have stayed at The Inn Above Tide on Sausalito, but those prices are astronomical. Disregarding the construction site, we enjoyed our view on Jefferson Street, and would pick this room again.Our bay view room had a couch and ottoman, which we thought was terrific. So nice just for relaxing after a hard day of walking and shopping. We appreciated the wine-tasting hour, although we missed it both nights. I also liked the Aveda products as I use them, and therefore didn't have to bring mine.Another thing I liked was the couches  comfy chairs in the lobby. Checkout was at noon, and after we had lunch, we had several hours to kill before taking our limo to the airport (we in fact used the Argonaut's limo instead of calling our rental company). There are chaise lounges as well and even though I didn't think the lounges were terribly comfortable, the huge chairs made for a great nap!I only have two negative things to say and neither of them are deal breakers on staying again...there were no free premium t.v. channels such as HBO. Even at cheaper hotels, you normally get this amenity. TV was just the normal cable faire which wasn't too thrilling. The 2nd item was just annoying - after our room had been made up (early in the day), we came back, got comfy for the night and heard a knock on the door - my husband had to get dressed only to find it was staff wanting to check the honor bar - we were none too happy, and told him to come back later. This is something that could have been checked when they made up the room. In fact, it should have been done as they were making up the room. We didn't use the honor bar but we did bring in our own wine, and so far haven't received any type of charge because the staff thought we were using theirs.As always we enjoyed dinner at Scouma's (the Shellfish Saute is wonderful and there's so much food you can't possibly eat it all); we took the ferry to Sausalito for the day (great art galleries and shopping); walked to Pier 39 (more great shopping), and had a fabulous dinner on Friday evening (as suggested by the concierge) at Ana Mandara at Ghiradelli Square. This is a French-Vietnamese fusion restaurant with live music (very subdued), wonderful ambience, and food that will knock your socks off. Try the Vietnamese Crispy Rolls (appetizer), the Banana Blossom Salad with Chicken and Grapefruit (to die for); the Organic Baby Greens with Ginger Dressing is also wonderful. My husband had the Roasted Duck Breast with Tamarind Sauce and Poached Banana Blossom, and I had the Spicy Garlic Prawns (they weren't hot-spicy at all) with Tamarind Sauce  Corn Cake (beware, you only get 4 prawns) and the dish was $28.00! Skip dessert, and get the Vietnamese Coffee - it's dessert in a glass.We are used to the prices in California (and elsewhere) and know that eating out is just plain expensive. We did get coffee at Starbucks around the corner from the Argonaut, had Irish Coffee at Buena Vista (across from Starbucks) and also had breakfast at the Buena Vista because they were supposed to have bountiful breakfasts. Well we spent over $30, and the breakfast was anything but bountiful! The Irish Coffee, though, was terrific and I don't like whiskey.We had dinner in the Blue Mermaid (restaurant in the Argonaut) on Saturday evening because we were just too bushed to go anywhere else. I had the Crab Louis salad and my husband had their fish/chips (skip this dish). We started off with an appetizer of calamari, and the dish was so huge, we should have quit with that. My salad was also quite large, although a tad salty for my taste. The wait staff were very nice and helpful.All in all, I'd say our annual trip to San Franciso was a hit and made memorable by the Argonaut - we've already marked the date for next year, and will be returning.A note about the weather - San Francico's weather can be hit or miss, and of course, when you're near the water, it's always cooler. Last year we were there in March, and it was warmer than this year, 45 days later. Next year, I think we may try for May. It was only in the high 50s yesterday, and we were not prepared (only having light blazers).

Rather than repeat all the previous reviews, I will just say that this is a great hotel, great location, clean rooms, and great service!Just a little background of who I am and why I went there that might help you compare your needs and desires when considering this hotel.We wanted a weekend getaway with my kids, boy-8 and girl-6. Me I am a 40 yr old self employed enterprenuer in the automotive design industry. I like hi-tech, good design, descent service and presentation. This hotel satisfied all that. I don't need to be waited on hand and foot (fetch my ice for me please) nor do I demand it because I am a guest.... I expect that if I am a descent human being and treat others similarly, that they will do the same for me. I only say this because SOME... NOT ALL of the less favorable reviews, on this site in general, maybe coming from these demanding kind of people.... the spoiled rotten.My kids and I just like to go places and see cool things. This location offered just that. Being by the water and w/in walking distance to many sites and attractions, this hotel was perfect for us. One thing we did that I would recommend if you can afford it, was we rented the lil electric car and went for a cruise around the city on one of their preplanned, gps guided, routes. Kids loved the open feel of the car too. Not the most powerful thing on the planet but perfect for a leisure cruise. The route we took was the 1 hour deal that took us to the base of the Golden Gate Bridge and down Lombard (famous crooked, twisty road) over to Coit Tower. Great veiws along the way and some cool runs up and down the hills of SF. AND the car does make it up the steepest of hills.... even though it didn't feel like it would.... phewCable car is right next door too. WARNING.... This one is a crap shoot in that going f/ the hotel is easy since you board at the beginning of the line, getting back is not. Many of the cars, on the return route, were packed full of tourists. This was only the middle of April too.... hate to see what it would be like during peak season. Also, weekends are WAY MORE congested than weekdays. Try a weekday morning early afternoon for a better chance at getting back to the hotel. An alternative on the weekends is that there are limos, running the same route as the cable cars, who will offer you a ride back to the hotel or Fisherman's Warf area for the same price as a cable car fare ($3.00 / person 5 yrs +). Beat the heck out of walking!!!! and the kids dug the 6 passenger stretch.That's pretty much it.. .the rest is a walk away.... Fisherman's Warf, Pier 39 (lot's of shops and restaurants) to the right as you exit the hotel and Ghiradelli Sq and cable car to the left and some old boats and stores straight ahead. If you want a nice clean place to stay.... a true 4 star property, then the Argonaut is your place to hang in SF. Enjoy! Got any questions.... email me and I'll be happy to answer. Oh... one last tip... have the doorman hire you a towncar to SFO (or other airports). For $5 bucks more than a cab.... it is a much nicer way to depart on your way home or wherever.... yup.... only $5 bucks!

<Author>John_in_UK
<Content>OTT nautical theme! Stayed here for 1 night at the end of our trip. It's at the quiet end of the Fisherman's Wharf, where tacky souvenir shops give way to open spaces and greenery. Our standard room was a generous size with a comfortable bed  a ludicrously sized nautical mirror  was furnished to a high standard. The exposed brick  beams give real character to the rooms. The wine reception was a lovely feature but, as others have noted, it was sad to clearly watch people walk in from the street, help themselves, and walk out again. The room was pretty noisy - not only the music from the Cannery courtyard (during the afternoon) but unusually so from corridors and adjoining rooms.We stayed here  at The Orchard near Union Square. Both are great hotels but for a holiday exploring the city I would much prefer to stay at The Orchard (which is close to all major transport links around the city) and take the fun cable car ride to Fisherman's wharf than to base myself here.

<Author>creto
<Content>Unprofessional It's a real shame that the Argonaut is probably the nicest hotel I've ever stayed at, but upon checkout we were charged an additional $21.00 for beer. Apparently the cleaning staff noticed empty beer cans in the room and assumed that we had taken them out of the minibar, which we didn't open even once during our stay. We bought beer at a local market and brought it back to our room. We explained this to the staff when we checked out, and they told us that they would remove this bogus charge, but when I got my credit card bill, the charge was still there. Most hotels have a better way of keeping up with what's taken out of minibars. My suggestion is that if you stay at the Argonaut and don't plan to use the minibar, return your key to it immediately. Don't get caught in their trap.I paid enough just to stay at this hotel, and to be charged even one penny extra is an insult. But to be lied to by the hotel staff goes beyond thunderdome.And a word to the cleaning staff: I left you a generous tip because I thought you did such a great job cleaning the room each day. However, because of you, I will never leave a tip again in a hotel room, and believe me, I will never stay at the Argonaut again.

<Author>tetheredincolorado
<Content>Very solid hotel! Our family of 4 stayed at the Argonaut for 3 nights. My husband then stayed there for a meeting for another 2 nights after the rest of us returned home. THE GOOD/GREAT:The location absolutely cannot be beaten! It is within EASY, flat, walking distance to everything Fisherman's Wharf has to offer (Ghirardelli Square, Alcatraz, Pier 39, the Hyde Street turnaround for cable cars, the Cannery, and numerous cute restaurants and shops.).The architectural detail and interior design is fun, unique and very nautical. As it is located in a renovated, brick, warehouse built many, many years ago. The room we had contained 2 thick, wooden, original, ceiling/wall support beams. The exterior wall was also made of the original brick. The wall paper, fixtures and furnishings were bright and elegantly fun. It was very unique and wonderful for a hotel room.Our room faced east and overlooked the attractive courtyard of the Cannery. There was live music going on from noonish- about 7 or 8:00 each day. As our windows did, in fact, open (another plus in my book!) we felt like we had our own entertainment.Taxis were easy to hail from the entrance.The GOOD/AVERAGE:As the hotel is really a large rectangle with a rectangular, courtyard on the interior, 1/2 of the rooms are on the interior and look out onto the other interior rooms. The bottom of the courtyard is actually just the ugly roof of the lobby. My husband found this out when he switched to a kingbed room after the rest of us left. So, if you want the effect of the very cool, brick outer wall and any kind of view, request an EXTERIOR facing room.The bellmen seemed a little overwhelmed. They were very polite and took our luggage as soon as we got there which was WELL before check-in time. They did, however, sometimes seem not to be attentive in terms of seeing us coming and opening the doors for us. In fact, sometimes they were all so busy trying to get people's cars for them that there were none there at all...and forget about them hailing a cab for you. That's YOUR job.Parking was a whopping 36 dollars per day PLUS another $5.95 parking tax which they don't tell you about. Yes, San Francisco is expensive, but just parking at the hotel cost more per day than our full sized rental. That annoyed me sort of in the same way that WAY overpriced hotel restaurants annoy me. There's just a point where the price just seems unreasonable and like a slap in the face....but I digress.... Count on 15-30 minutes for the valet's to get your car from wherever it is that they park them. Apparently, it was BLOCKS away. This delay was consistently the case for us. They did, in all fairness however, warn us to expect 15 minutes.All in all, I'd be hardpressed to stay elsewhere in San Francisco. No place is perfect, but the Argonaut is wonderful!

<Author>jpsanpedro
<Content>Great stay at the Argonaut We stayed at the Argonaut hotel between the 4th and 7th of January, as part of a combined business  vacation trip. While I'm sure my wife and I have stayed at better hotels (more services, more luxurious fixtures, etc.) I can't recall having ever stayed at a hotel we liked more. - The staff was always friendly and positive, even when helping us search for some shoes we thought we lost upon arrival at 1am (but actually had in our bags all along)- The location is stunning. If you're thinking of going to SF with your dog, stay here.- Terrific bed! (Much better than the otherwise enjoyable Hotel Burnham in Chicago.)- Interesting but not overbearing decoration. As much as I love Kimptons, their decor can get a bit gaudy. The nautical theme worked well, especially with the exposed beams of the old building visible.- Amenities galore. Even by Kimpton standards, these were often a cut higher: Aveda and free high speed internet of course, plus DVD players in every room, free (Fetzer!) wine in the evenings, free car service in the a.m.- We got all of this for a very reasonable rate, but even at a much higher price it would still be a good deal.Areas for improvement:- They charge $5 to deliver a package to your room. C'mon guys, that's absurd.- No coffee service in the morning? Every other Kimpton offers this.- Sometimes the guidance of the friendly and positive staff was a bit lacking, as when they twice gave incorrect driving directions to the Ferry Building.- The food, selection, and prices of room service are really lacking.These issues, however, are no match for the overwhelming positives that make Argonaut so terrific.

<Author>QVCAddict
<Content>Soundproofing is desperately needed The majority of our stay at the Argonaut hotel was wonderful. The location of the hotel was fantastic. It was right on fisherman's wharf, and within walking distance of the attractions. Because of the hotel's convenient location we were able to board our tour of the city right in front of the hotel instead of driving to the tour company's main office. We enjoyed visiting the maritime museum, which was located inside the hotel. The bellmen, and doormen were friendly and helpful. They unloaded our baggage and two wheelchairs from our car, and assisted us into the hotel lobby. The nautical inspired decor in the lobby and in our room was beautiful. There were a lot of cute, whimsical decorations, and design elements in our room. We absolutely loved it. Our room and bathroom were wheelchair accessible and easy to navigate through. The seafood at the hotel restaurant was wonderful, and we liked the casual atmosphere. The hotel unfortunately has one MAJOR flaw. The rooms are not at all adequately soundproofed. At around 2am I was watching television. I had the volume turned down low as not to disturb my grandmother and aunt who were sleeping in the bed next to mine. But to my surprise, the people in the next room started banging on the wall, and shouting for me to turn down the volume on the television. I turned the volume on the television down to the point where I had to sit next to the television to hear the sound. I was annoyed at having to do this, but thought that it would solve the problem. To my surprise I received an unpleasant phone call from the hotel's front desk asking me to turn the volume down on the television. The television would have had to be OFF for the volume to be any lower. Up until that point, the hotel environment was warm and comfortable. After that incident I felt very uncomfortable staying there. I will not return to the Argonaut until they fix their sound issues.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Wonderful hotel...book now! Just returned from a four night stay at The Argonaut. The hotel is situated in the best bit of Fisherman's Wharf. On the whole the Wharf is tacky, but not as bad as I expected. The proximity to the cable car stop is a definate bonus (especially if you are on your own and worried about safety).The staff were friendly at all times and always acknowledged you, and you always received a friendly welcome from the doorman. The decor, although wacky, is very tasteful and not at all overpowering.I had a room facing the courtyard (a view would have been nice, but I was hardly in the room during daylight hours). It was totally spotless, you would honestly think that it had been furnished and renovated especially for your visit. Lots of extra touches that set the hotel apart, such as flat screen TV, DVD, Starbucks coffee, modern phone and clock radio. Free internet in the lobby was a huge benefit and was not abused. Ate breakfast in the hotel a few mornings and was impressed with the food and the service (unlike some other reviewers.)I would definately return to The Argonaut on my next visit to San Francisco- during my time there I saw no other hotel that I would rather stay in. If you plan on staying at the Wharf, stay here. The other chain hotels (Holiday Inn, Radisson etc) look run down and dated from the outside.

<Author>LucyKate
<Content>Magnificent There's a very good reason this place is at the top of this list - it is absolutely magnificent.Superb location - right across the road from the wharves, right next to the Cable Car, views of the Bridge, but it's what they have done with this location that makes it superb.The hotel is in a restored warehouse, and the attention to detail throughout is wonderful with exposed beams and bricks making this a standout building. Only 1 gripe - leave the car at home or ensure your room rate includes parking - they charge $32 a day!A truly wonderful hotel.

The nautical d茅cor was interesting; cute for families but not exactly my taste.Some of the pros: Good location - While we were within comfortable walking distance to Fisherman鈥檚 Wharf and good restaurants (go to Gary Danko!), it was still in a very quiet and safe location. The bathrooms were unimpressive but I liked the Aveda products. The beds were comfortable and topped with fluffy pillows and comforters. The Sony TV and DVD player was a nice touch, as was the free high speed internet connection. As for price, it was pretty affordable (our price was $150/night) for what you get.Now for the bad stuff: The walls were a bit thin as we could hear our neighbors or people outside our door chatting away. Each time we drove to the hotel, the valet guy was nowhere to be found so had to leave our car (locked up of course) at curbside and gave our keys to the front desk person. Finally, the remote control for the TV was actually the Nintendo game control and therefore the only way to change channels was to go up or down. It also didn鈥檛 help that it was not wireless.All in all, I鈥檇 suggest this hotel if you鈥檙e an out of town cost-conscious tourist especially interested in exploring the Fisherman鈥檚 Wharf area. One suggestion to the hotel 鈥?Sounds like being turned away for not having a room available has happened frequently in the past. Rather than letting your guests show up and be disappointed, you should proactively call and let them know beforehand so they can go directly to another hotel. This might also save your front staff from verbal abuse.

<Author>martdm
<Content>Argonaut A+ Just returned from a 5 day stay at the Argonaut Hotel. We had two rooms purchased for $123 a night through Hotwire.We found this hotel to be an excellent choice for anyone wishing to be in the Fisherman's Wharf vicinity. It is on the edge of Jefferson Street, adjacent to the Cannery  Maritime Museum and although walking distance to Pier 39 and all other attractions between (about 15 blocks) it is on a more quiet end of the street, away from the bars  tourist stores. The streetcars are a block away and the historic trolleys are kitty corner behind the hotel. It's truly a very restful and scenic stretch of the Wharf.The hotel itself is very attractive in it's ship themeing, with lovely plank wood floors, rich red, blue, and golds in the fabrics  carpets, and rich wood fixtures elsewhere. Our queen/queen rooms were typical in their layout (beds, nightstands, desk, tv stand) but very appealing with the exposed brick wall of the original structure on one end, weathered tables, excellent linens, decorative pillows, and the ever present nautical theming. The bath was typically sized and had a generous countertop, shower massager, plenty of nice towels, and luxury bath products. Housekeeping took impeccable care of the room each day.The staff was friendly and efficient, with some members of the front door and bell staff going well out of their way to provide advice, guidance, special services, and friendly conversation when we waited out front for our group or the valet.The only hitch in an otherwise top-notch stay was the front desk failing to relay our request to have our cars brought around on the day of our departure (at least that's what the valet claimed). Because this delayed us nearly 1/2 hour, we had a rather frantic drive to the airport and sprint to the ticket counter to make our flight. I'm not sure where the communication breakdown actually occurred and I only mention it as a word to the wise since it did cause some stress, but it really was a small blemish on an otherwise terrific experience. I highly recommend this hotel, their staff, the service, and the location.

<Author>oohthathurts
<Content>Argonaut Hotel is great hotel Just returned from San Fransico. Argonaut stay was great! Location was great. Service was excellent. Strikers are not only picketing but banging pots and pans and running sirens from 7:00 a.m. til 10:00 p.m. Most of the striking hotels are downtown though there are a few near Fishemans Wharf. Union square is VERY noisy. If you are planning a stay there I recommend you check with hotel to see if they are affected. Fortunately for us though everything was quiet at the Argonaut. The people at the Argonaut are cheerful, polite and friendly. We had a room on the inner court so heard no street noise at all. Could hear people in the hall occasionally and now and then in the closet but that was it. The hotel offers a wine reception from 5 to 6. They don't verify you are staying at hotel so this is sometimes pretty busy. The wine thing was nice but free breakfast would probably have been better.The hotel provides Aveda soaps, shampoo and conditioner. Very nice. Leaves a great aromal in the room. Entering the room was alway a nice treat. The room size was nice as well. I frequently wished the room had a balconey as it would have been nice to just sit outside and relax. However, this is San Fransico. Do rooms like that exist?I would stay at Argonaut again. Definately learned to ask if hotel is union and if so are they in negotiation process.

The vast majority of reviews can't be wrong, and for anyone who gives it two stars, would you want them staying in the same hotel as you? No I don't either, let them go and pay the chain hotels more money for less.

<Author>!!
<Content>Family Friendly with Loads of Character Stayed at The Argonaut for a week in April 2004. Everything still fresh and new which greatly enhanced stay - we had a fabulous time. Room was huge and very comfortable. Aveda products in bathroom. Room service comprehensive but expensive ... just as easy to go downstairs to excellent Blue Mermaid restaurant; great chowders and children's menu. Decor a little bit Disney-esque but all very good quality and offset against the exposed brick walls it works very well. The hotel has bags of character and seemed to us to be quite unique amoungst the rather faceless big hotels in SF. The Argonaut is child friendly - our five year old son was made to feel very welcome. The staff were without exception dazzlingly helpful and professional; we really got the impression that they were proud of The Argonaut. Valet parking is pricey but very convenient; the one time they took a while to find the car the charge was taken off the bill (without us asking) Location perfect for exploring the city; it is noisy and parts of Fisherman's Wharf are rather tacky but everything is within easy reach. Maybe in time the gloss will fade a little at The Argonaut - the furnishings get a bit tattier and the staff more jaded; we'd love to go back some time to see if they can maintain the momentum!!Cannot recommend this hotel highly enough especially if you have children in tow.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Stay at the Argonaut Stayed at the Argonaut four nights August 19-23. While Fisherman's Wharf is too touristy and restaurant choices there are limited, it is still the place to stay on a first visit with kids. And the Argonaut was a great choice. Room was large and clean, beds were very comfortable (best beds on our trip), common areas are very nice and the location on Fisherman's Wharf can't be beat. A bit away from all the really tacky stuff with the National Maritime Historic Park and cable car line right across the street. As previous reviewers have noted, hotel is a little noisy, but nothing unusual for an urban hotel. We thought the Concierge and staff services were great (my kids got a charge when the doorman held the door open for them) and the breakfast in the Blue Mermaid was also good. (A little pricey, but not out of line with local prices.) Bill was incorrect at checkout with an erroneous honor bar charge, but this was quickly corrected. Would stay there again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Location, Location, Location!!! We just returned from a 4 night stay at the Argonaut. As our ride pulled up to the hotel the bell hop rushed out to get out luggage and welcome us to the hotel. We checked in and were on our way to our room. The rooms are long and somewhat narrow. The room has a nice size bathroom with tile and marble, Aveda shampoo and conditioner and lotion, 4 cup coffee pot with Starbucks coffe and Tazo tea, the hair dryer is in a bag that hangs on a hook by the shower. The shower was great, the towels were fluffy and soft. There is a nice desk with plenty of plug ins, nice size closet with a safe and plenty of wood hangers. The bed was very comfy, down comforter and a great blanket. There is a great flat screen tv, honor bar and lounger couch. We chose and interior room from what we had read here. The room was quite. You do hear other peoples doors closing and once in a while you may hear someone in the hall. We had our airconditioner going the whole time so we did not hear much. I did not care about the view, I was not there to hang out in my room. The Blue Mermaid restuarant is pretty good. The best food we had was at Nona Rose's down by pier 39 also at Cipponios, just down the street. There is a bike rental place just at the cannery by the hotel. The cannery is right next door and on weekends they have bands, we sat at Jack's which has 85 different beers on tap. I would say the only down fall to our stay, was that our Honor bar was never restocked and some of the candy in it was old. My husband just went to the liquor store down the street and bought his own beer. All and All I was VERY pleased with the hotel and would stay there again, the location really makes it. The Wharf is very touristy, if you want nice shops go to Market street. We walked from the hotel to China Town, make sure you have good walking shoes, the hills are killer. If you go in August, bring jeans and sweaters or sweatshirts, it does get cool. We rented bikes from Blazing Saddles and biked across the Golden Gate Bridge into Socileto (SP) what a cute town, ate at a great sushi bar called Sushi Row. What a great trip
