<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Lovely hotel, terrible location How do you write a review of a very good hotel that happens to be located in an area that you absolutely hate? We stayed at The Argonaut for 4 nights in July 2004. It is quite a fancy hotel in a renovated warehouse adjacent to the Cannery at the end of the main drag in Fisherman's Wharf. The decor is nautical and some of the original details like wooden beams and iron rivets have been kept intact. The rooms have bathrobes, coffeemakers, refrigerators, and safes but are fairly small. We had requested a room with two queen-size beds but were told upon arrival that no such room was available. Instead we were offered a king-size bed with a roll-away for our daughter at an extra cost of $20 for the entire stay. We were told that some king-size rooms did not accommodate a roll-away, but that ours did. However, I doubt that was true because our room got extremely crowded with the roll-away in it. We also had to ask twice to get the roll-away delivered to our room.On the plus side was a spacious fitness room with up-to-date equipment, free Internet access from two computers in the common area, and a daily complementary wine reception in what is pretentiously called the living room (read: reception area; I guess the fire place is supposed to give it a more homey feeling). The staff was professional and courteous, albeit a bit impersonal.This was our first time in San Francisco and had we realized how much we would hate Fisherman's Wharf (have never seen such a concentration of tourist shlock anywhere), we would never have chosen The Argonaut despite its many fine qualities.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Very disappointed I stayed at the Argonaut in early July based on recommendations in this and other forums. I would not recommend this hotel for anyone seeking a quiet or romantic spot or a luxury property. The hotel was packed with families and the walls are thin. We could hear all of the family noise from the room next door. The lobby was full of teen-agers and family groups. The teens monopolized the two computers in the lobby. Since this is a feature highlighted by the hotel, they should provide more computers.The staff was extremely young. This might have been their first job. When I asked about switching rooms after the first night of our 4 night stay, they said that the family next to us was checking out that day so we decided not to switch rooms. They actually checked out the following day. And guess what, the next occupant of the room next to ours also had young noisy children. But at that point we were unpacked so it wasn't worth switching and besides we weren't in the room all that much. The lobby was OK, but not what I expected from a 4 star hotel. For what we paid a night, I expected a more spacious room and more luxury in the lobby. The rooms are strange; we had a deluxe king, which meant we had a view. However our room was a rectangular shape, long and narrow. Very narrow. The bathroom didn't have a normal locking door; it was a pocket door. This didn't matter to my husband and me but it is weird. The bathroom itself was fine. The bed was very comfortable. The best thing about the room was that it had a multi-outlet surge protector power strip into which we could plug in (to recharge) all of our various equipment (2 cell phones, digital camera, Blackberry, and laptop). As we travel, we find that most hotel rooms do not have sufficient outlets.The nautical motif was fine, but taken to the extreme. Our room and bathroom didn't have to be shaped and outfitted like a ship's room. The location was very good in that it was at the end of the Wharf so it is not as busy as other hotels. It was convenient to the cable car and buses. The Wharf is tacky and touristy but sometimes that can be fun, depending what you are looking for.The reason I am posting this is that a traveler seeking top accomodations at Fisherman's Wharf may be better off staying at the Hilton or Hyatt. I got to believe that they cost less money and the rooms are larger and quieter.I think this hotel would be fine for families with teens or for travelers who don't expect sophistication, quiet, and exlusiveness in a four star hotel.

We don't often participate in hotel wine tastings while we're on vacation, but we made a point to be at the fireplace in the Argonaut's lobby by 5:00 just to enjoy the camaraderie and the ambiance of the place. Also, our room was a delight. The bed was the most comfortable we've ever had in a hotel, the linens were wonderful, and the leopard pattern bathrobes were a nice touch. Enough has already been written about the outstanding interior design details. We join the crowd in rating it a 10. Amaxingly, all of this comes at a reasonable price! Rates at run-of-the mill chain hotels in Wine Country cost more than we paid at the Argonaut. I can't wait to go back and to try other hotels in the Kimpton Group.

<Author>djkbooks
<Content>Fabulous in every way... From the moment we were met at the door when we drove up, we found the service at this hotel exceptionally friendly and helpful, throughout, all during our stay. We also found the hotel beautiful and comfortable. At first, I thought the nautical theme and decor a bit excessive, but grew to enjoy it enormously during our stay.The reception area is warm and inviting, along with the enormous 鈥渓iving room鈥?with fireplace. For once, our room looked exactly like the one in the photo (except for the view out the window) on the website! Our room was quite spacious with a truly comfortable bed (very nice linens, awesome comforter, plenty of wonderful pillows with more in the closet) and a sitting area with a couch with a large desk in between (with free high speed internet access). The (27 Sony flat screen) TV was atop a large cabinet and swivelled to be viewed perfectly from either the bed or the couch. All our favorite cable stations were available. The cabinet had drawers on one side and a spacious refrigerator on the other side (with space for your own things, or you could remove honor bar items for even more space). The large bathroom was all tile and marble and very nicely appointed with a coffee pot (Starbucks coffee), Aveda products and plenty of large, thick, white towels (with no bleach aroma whatsoever). It was very well lit and there was also a magnifying makeup mirror and blow dryer (not attached to the wall, so you could dry your hair elsewhere if you liked). Terrific shower head (adjustable) with plenty of hot water and pressure. The sizeable closet contained a safe, plenty of nice wooden hangers (with regular hooks), along with an iron and ironing board.This room had the finest lighting of any we鈥檝e ever experienced. Among the many, perfectly located (without impossible to figure out switches) lamps was a lovely large tubular lamp with dimmer switch (fabulous, oh so romantic!). The desk lamp and the reading lamps on either side of the bed were 3-way. Climate control was excellent. The casement window (covered with terrific louvered shutters for breezes with privacy) opened for fresh air.There was a huge (6' or larger?) convex 鈥減orthole鈥?mirror on the wall opposite the bed which, along with the lamp with the dimmer switch, rendered the 鈥渆xperience鈥?quite atmospheric!Housekeeping was meticulous. Each time I left a note, my request was fulfilled. Room service was swift with our order beautifully presented, with food (breakfast) that was excellent and not outrageously priced.Though our room faced Beach Street, and there was a sidewalk right underneath our window, the street noise was minimal. Some rooms have 鈥渧iews鈥? I would suggest insisting that your room not be on the interior, where all views are of a concrete courtyard and the windows of other room windows. Note also that the hotel is an entire city block long, so your room (our was) could be quite a hike from the elevators.Though we鈥檝e never had the urge to stay in the Fisherman鈥檚 Wharf neighborhood, we loved the location of the Argonaut. It鈥檚 at the far western edge just half a block from the Powell/Hyde cable car turnaround (and another half block from the Buena Vista Caf茅!). There were convenient bus/streetcar routes to everywhere (Downtown, the Embarcadero, Cow Hollow, Marina...) nearby, and finding a taxi was never a problem. A Rite-Aid (with soda, water, etc.) was two blocks away, along with a Starbucks.The hotel is part of the Cannery with many dining opportunities, and many more in every direction (Restaurant Gary Danko is two blocks away). The boat, bus, motorized cable car, tours are all within blocks.The Blue Mermaid restaurant within the hotel is very (very) casual with a moderately priced menu of appealing offerings (including half a dozen or more chowders served in bread bowls) and tables set outdoors in the courtyard of the Cannery.Though there is no cocktail lounge (and the restaurant closes at 9PM week nights, 10PM Friday and Saturday), there are lots of nice places (including the aforementioned Buena Vista Caf茅 - famous for their Irish Coffee) nearby.I joined my husband during a business trip (he stayed at the Concord Hilton before and after) for four nights. Once at the Argonaut, however, I wished I had planned a longer stay!We found this hotel enormously beautiful, comfortable and appealing in every way. We do not appreciate or favor fancy, or swanky, or way sleek, or stuffy, so the Argonaut was perfect for us.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice hotel but somewhat noisy I stayed at the hotel on Friday, July 23. The hotel was very nice, and the staff was very friendly. I loved the Nautica theme! The rooms were nice sized, but I woke up at 6:30 a.m. when the guests in the adjacent room got up. I could hear almost every word of their conversation, and they were speaking at a normal level. Also, the ice machine was three to four doors down, and it's behind a door. However, it's necessary for the door to be open to access the ice, and you could hear it whenever somebody got ice. Parking was $32.00 per day, which was slightly above what appears to be an average rate of $25.00 per day for San Francisco. After paying the room rate, taxes and parking, the room came to about $355.00 for one night. For just a little more than half that amount, I would opt for the Grosvenor Suites Hotel, which is older and does not have a lobby to speak of. However, if you're looking for a good location and a nice size room for a reasonable price, I would recommend the Grosvenor Suites. If you're looking to impress somebody, then I would stay at the Argonaut Hotel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>All The Good Reviews Are True I researched many hotels before my husband and I traveled to San Francisco on May 19-22. The Argonaut received great reviews and I couldn't agree with them more. This hotel is a converted factory in the same complex with the historic Cannery. It's brick walls and huge timber beams add a lot of character to the large rooms. The pictures of the rooms show the nautical theme. My only concern was that the rooms would be death by theme and resemble some hokey Disney resort. Not at all. The rooms are very tastefully decorated and the nautical theme ties into the hotel's fabulous location - near the Wharf and across from the Hyde Street Pier and Nautical Museum. Across the street is the historic turn-around for the Hyde-Powell cable car line. Our room had a great view out of the large plantation shutters down to a quaint park. There is a nice and casual restaurant on premise, The Blue Mermaid. For breakfast, check out the dive restaurants right behind the hotel that serve excellent waffles and pancakes (Off North Point). Everything you could want is within walking distance, including Ghiradelli Square a block or so away. I can't forget the ever friendly staff who were very professional, the wine tastings in the afternoon, the Aveda products, and you will not find a more comfortable hotel bed anywhere. The only thing that went wrong was that I almost got charged with valet parking when we did not even pick up our rental car until check-out, but as I was about to sign the charges without even reviewing them, the clerk asked me to please double-check all of the charges and then immediately credited the erroneous charges. This hotel is outstanding.

<Author>corgimomDallas
<Content>a rare find on the whart I almost hate to write this review, knowing that this little known hotel will start to be fully booked once the word is out. The newest and closest hotel to the wharf (right across the street). I thoroughly enjoyed getting up early, going to Starbucks (two blocks down) and walking down to the pier to watch the sea lions and the fog before everyone else was out and about. The doorman at the Argonaut was wonderful. The front desk staff was a little young, but helpful. The lobby (just off the maritime museum foyer) is warm and cozy with a fireplace and lots of couches and chairs. I enjoyed the nautical decor in the rooms - the space reminds you of a cruise ship with long and narrow rooms, and a wonderful huge porthole mirror on the wall. The bath is a little small, but the pocket door helps you navigate the space. the robe and makeup mirror were extra nice touches. No view from my room, but I never spend much time looking out the window when I can go outside and smell the salty air. Beds were comfy and crisp. The Chowder house attached isn't anything to rave about (almost a serve-yourself place) but the italian restaurant across the street is wonderful. The rates were unbelievably low for the wharf area - under $150. We'll definitely stay there again.

<Author>mkdevereaux
<Content>Disappointed The Argonaut's location is fantastic. The beds are very comfortable. The decor is beautiful, albeit a bit sterile. Easter Sunday is a great day to be in SF at the Argonaut, because the crowds are very light. That said, our disappointment with the Argonaut began within minutes of our arrival. We arrived at 10 am, which apparently is the staff's coffee break, because the doorman was nowhere in sight when I struggled through the door with luggage. Although the hotel offers an upgrade incentive to book directly with them online, when I asked about it, I was told that there was no upgrade available, although the hotel appeared to be no more than half full, if that. Our room 402, on the top floor of the hotel, overlooked a busy street and the parking garage, rather than the courtyard view I booked online. A very noisy garbage pickup began at 4:30 am and lasted forever. Then, large trucks started rumbling by with deliveries for Fisherman's wharf. Sleep was impossible. While all of that may change from day to day, what won't change is the lack of any seating other than the beds and one desk chair in the standard deluxe room. For a luxury hotel, where the cheapest room was $169, I expect a chair to sit on, at minimum.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Close and Cozy We experienced a wonderful stay at the Argonaut; February 15-18. The hotel is loud in design, but cozy in itself. The bold nautical design didn't bother us a bit, in fact, we felt it added to the fun atmosphere. We felt we had chosen the right hotel for our needs, and are glad we did. We had originally wanted to stay at the Pan Pacific... but then decided to stay closer to where we were going to be most of the time... Fisherman's Wharf and Pier 39. Good thing we did! Ghirardelli's Square is pretty much around the corner. Cable cars are across the street. Lombard is five blocks up a very steep hill... but managable if you take it slowly! I do have to warn you though... Pier 39 and 41 aren't as close as other reviews seem to make them. Fisherman's Wharf is about 3 block away... add another 3 blocks for Pier 39 and 41. It's about a 15 minute walk, each way. I think our problem was that we were there on a holiday weekend, and the streets were packed. Perhaps it wouldn't have been so bad if we chose to go at a different time. Once we got past the weekend though, it was really nice. We found a great deal on Expedia... but didn't book through them because Kimpton will match online rates as long as they are verifiable at the time of booking. Plus, they give you an automatic room upgrade for booking through them. So, we booked an interior room, for $103,and got one with a view instead... Nice! The rooms are NARROW, and loooong. The down comforter and pillows are a super nice touch... and the TV was great, nice and clear... had to touch it to see if it was plasma. Bathrooms are stocked with Aveda products... another nice addition. The hotel staff is great! John, the doorman during the days, is absolutly friendly! Pascal, and the other gal at concierge are super sweet, and knowledgeable. This was our first time in San Francisco, and they gave us all the info we needed, when we wanted it! Ed on the other hand (the other concierge) could stand to be a bit less stuffy. I'm surprised they haven't needed to repaint the cieling from his nose scraping it! All in all we were pleased with the Argonaut, and plan on going back soon. We will definitley stay here again! Visit our website for a few pictures of the Argonaut and the surrounding area! http://www.resorthoppers.com/SanFrancisco

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great location and friendly staff! My husband and I stayed at the Argonaut the weekend of February 14, 2004. We were treated very well by the Argonaut staff. The location was the best for the Fisherman's Wharf area. The hotel is located in the old cannery across from Ghirardelli square and across the street from the Buena Vista (where the first Irish coffee was invented). The hotel beds are extremely comfortable and the rooms are super clean. The only downside (there is one to everything) is that the rooms with the queen size beds are a little small, so if you are looking for more space, upgrade to the king. The best is that the lovely Cioppinos restaurant is also across the street. Pier 39 is not super close, but is within walking distance. This is the only place I would stay in San Francisco. We go a couple of times a year and I have stayed in other places in the area and they do not even compete.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Absolutely Great! Just returned from 5 nights at the Argonaut Hotel, Jan 14 - 19, 2004. Researched more than 50 hotels in San Fran based on price, location, amenities and size. I felt I wanted to stay away from the noise of Union Square. I made my decision mostly from reviews by past guests. This hotel was everything the reviews and hotel web site stated. We asked for a room with a view of either Alcatraz or the GG Bridge. We were not disappointed. Every morning we awoke to a view of San Fran Bay. We paid $150 per night, AAA rate. The staff was excellent. Polite, professional and informative. The concierge was a huge help in making suggestions and assisting with reservations. The lobby was comfortable and had a nice fireplace to relax beside with a drink. This is a new hotel. It is located at Fisherman's Wharf, but at the end near Aquatic Park so it is quiet, but just a short walk to the hustle and bustle of Pier 39, the Grotto and other shops. Hotel resaurant was good. Parking was expensive at $32 per day. Taxi service was quick and plentiful. 1 minute walk to Hyde St. Cable car turnaround and Ghiradelli Sq. and 5 -10 minute walk to Pier 39, Alcatraz Ferry and other attractions. It was a great change from the Hilton, Hyatt, Sheraton routine. If your looking for a medium sized boutique hotel with great amenities at a fair price, this is it. Would stay here again in a heartbeat.

<Author>AprilB
<Content>Perfect location for us If you like nautical, the Argonaut is for you. The decor is fun and funky, the Maritime National Historical Park visitors center is off the lobby and the ships at Hyde St. Pier are across the street (you can tour several of them for a few $$). While I might not have normally chosen a Fishermans Wharf hotel for our stay, I felt this location was special. My husband and I loved it. The cable car turnaround is conveniently around the corner. From it, you can hop off to walk down crooked Lombard St., or visit the Cable Car Museum.Upon seeing the Golden Gate Bridge view room we had requested, we found the view of the bridge partially obscured by trees across the street. Also, my husband was concerned about traffic noise from vehicles accelerating up the hill, although this may not have been an issue at night. We switched to an Alcatraz view room (446) instead where the view was much more expansive, the room seemed brighter, and the square-rigged Balcutha was right out our window. Fabulous! The rooms we saw had either two queen-sized beds or one king and a couch. Both were clean and spacious with wallpapered and brick walls. The cooling/heating system in our room worked well and we found it very easy to control the temperature.We were told the inside rooms were quite small but, small or not, they have no view at all as they face a dismal-looking light well. The suites though, from what I saw from the hallway, must be quite large.Problems were minor. There was a bit of confusion with communication. Yes, you can definitely have a top floor, Golden Gate Bridge view room, to, No, we cant guarantee that. And, Yes, certainly you can have a late check out, to, No, we need that room to set up for an event. Ill bet I know exactly which doorman the TripAdvisor user from LA is talking about. He was the only employee we thought they could do without. Otherwise, the staff was bright, friendly and seemed bent on making our stay a pleasant one. Concierge staff was good too.If I were to stay again I would ask for bathrobes upon arrival since they weren't in our room. The heavy black and brown leopard spotted robes were comically out of place in a nautical themed environment.We found the food at the attached Blue Mermaid Chowder House to be so-so. Ghirardelli Square with McCormick and Kuleto's Restaurant and Loris Diner is a short walk away and they have similar terrific views as from the front of the Argonaut.Overall we had a delightful experience at the Argonaut and we would definitely stay there again.  
<Date>Oct 17, 2003
<Rating>5	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	

<Author>MrTed
<Content>Absolutely Fabulous! We just returned from a five night stay at the Argonaut (our first visit to San Francisco) and absolutely loved the hotel and the city. The hotel is located at Fisherman's Warf, directly across from the Hyde Street Pier and adjacent to the National Maritime Historic Park. The location is great -- you can walk to Pier 39 in less than 10 minutes, the cable car turnaround is one block behind the hotel, and Ghirardelli Square is about two blocks away. The hotel is new and very nice with a nautical theme throughout. The rooms are large with high ceilings (we were on the fourth floor) and great views of the Bay/Golden Gate Bridge/Alcatraz from the rooms on the front and west sides of the hotel. The staff was very friendly and helpful and responded quickly to all of our requests. We will definitely go back to San Francisco and the Argonaut.
